b\u00ean li\u00ean quan v\u00e0o c\u00e1c l\u0129nh v\u1ef1c kh\u00e1c nhau c\u1ee7a th\u1ecb tr\u01b0\u1eddng ti\u1ec1n \u0111i\u1ec7n t\u1eed nh\u1eb1m h\u01b0\u1edbng t\u1edbi vi\u1ec7c tri\u1ec3n khai MiCA m\u00e0 kh\u00f4ng g\u1eb7p tr\u1edf ng\u1ea1i n\u00e0o v\u00e0o n\u0103m 2024.\n\n\u2728C\u01a1 quan n\u00e0y s\u1ebd xem x\u00e9t t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 c\u00e1c \u0111\u1ec1 xu\u1ea5t c\u1ee7a cu\u1ed1i c\u00f9ng bao g\u1ed3m c\u00e1c khuy\u1ebfn ngh\u1ecb v\u00e0o qu\u00fd 1 n\u0103m 2024.\n\n  \ud83d\udc49 B\u00e0i vi\u1ebft nh\u1ea5n m\u1ea1nh n\u0103m l\u0129nh v\u1ef1c \u0111\u1ea7u (iii) offering pre-and post-trade data to the public; (iv) content and format of order book records and record-keeping by CASPs; (v) machine readability of white papers and the register of white papers; and (vi) the technical means for appropriate public disclosure of inside information.\u201d\u00a0\n\n      \ud83d\udccc ESMA \u0111\u01b0a ra \u0111\u1ec1 xu\u1ea5t v\u1ec1 c\u00e1c quy Nh\u01b0 v\u1eady \u0111\u1ee7 th\u1ea5y r\u1eb1ng Tr\u1ee5 V\u01b0\u01a1ng t\u1eebng l\u00e0 m\u1ed9t v\u1ecb vua l\u1ed7i l\u1ea1c v\u0103n v\u00f5 to\u00e0n t\u00e0i v\u00e0o thu\u1edf \u0111\u1ea7u l\u00ean ng\u00f4i.\n\nPhong Th\u1ea7n Di\u1ec5n Ngh\u0129a k\u1ec3 r\u1eb1ng m\u1ecdi bi\u1ebfn c\u1ed1 x\u1ea3y \u0111\u1ebfn b\u1eaft \u0111\u1ea7u t\u1eeb khi Tr\u1ee5 V\u01b0\u01a1ng t\u1edbi \u0111\u1ec1n th\u1edd b\u00e0 N\u1eef Oa \u0111\u1ec3 d\u00e2ng h\u01b0\u01a1ng v\u00e0 tr\u00f3t \u0111\u1ec1 th\u01a1 b\u1ea5t k\u00ednh v\u1edbi v\u1ecb n\u1eef Th\u1ea7n n\u00e0y. Vi\u1ec7c n\u00e0y c\u0169ng d\u01b0\u1eddng nh\u01b0 \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c \u0111\u1ecbnh s\u1ed1 t\u1eeb tr\u01b0\u1edbc, b\u1edfi v\u00ec Tr\u1ee5 V\u01b0\u01a1ng \u0111ang k\u00ednh ng\u01b0\u1ee1ng say m\u00ea ng\u1eafm nh\u00ecn \u0111\u1ebfn th\u1edd th\u00ec \u201cb\u1ed7ng m\u1ed9t lu\u1ed3n gi\u00f3 nh\u1eb9 th\u1ed5i qua l\u00e0m b\u1ee9c m\u00e0n v\u1eb9t qua, vua tr\u00f4ng th\u1ea5y t\u01b0\u1ee3ng b\u00e0 N\u1eef Oa r\u1ea5t r\u00f5\u201d (Tr\u00edch Phong Th\u1ea7n Di\u1ec5n Ngh\u0129a). T\u1eeb \u0111\u00f3 Tr\u1ee5 V\u01b0\u01a1ng m\u1edbi n\u1ea3y sinh d\u1ee5c v\u1ecdng v\u1edbi Th\u1ea7n, ph\u1ea1m t\u1ed9i b\u1ea5t k\u00ednh th\u1ea7n linh.\n\nN\u1eef Oa mu\u1ed1n b\u00e1o \u1ee9ng Tr\u1ee5 V\u01b0\u01a1ng, nh\u01b0ng khi t\u1edbi cung \u0111i\u1ec7n th\u00ec b\u1ecb h\u00e0o quang c\u1ea3n tr\u1edf. Phong Th\u1ea7n Di\u1ec5n Ngh\u0129a c\u00f3 vi\u1ebft r\u1eb1ng, trong m\u1ec7nh tr\u1eddi th\u00ec nh\u00e0 Th\u01b0\u01a1ng s\u1eafp \u0111\u1ebfn th\u1eddi di\u1ec7t vong, ch\u1ec9 l\u00e0 s\u1ed1 c\u00f2n ch\u01b0a h\u1ebft, c\u00f2n c\u00f3 hai m\u01b0\u01a1i t\u00e1m n\u0103m n\u1eefa, n\u00ean d\u00f9 th\u1ea7n th\u00f4ng qu\u1ea3ng \u0111\u1ea1i nh\u01b0 N\u1eef Oa c\u0169ng kh\u00f4ng th\u1ec3 tr\u00e1i m\u1ec7nh. \u0110\u1ed3ng th\u1eddi c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 th\u1ea5y sau n\u00e0y khi \u0111\u00e3 t\u1eadn s\u1ed1, d\u00f9 phe \u1ee7ng h\u1ed9 nh\u00e0 Th\u01b0\u01a1ng c\u00f3 t\u00e0i th\u00f4ng thi\u00ean \u0111\u1ebfn \u0111\u00e2u, Tru Ti\u00ean ki\u1ebfm tr\u1eadn c\u00f3 l\u1ee3i h\u1ea1i \u0111\u1ebfn m\u1ee9c \u0111\u1ed9 n\u00e0o, th\u00ec cu\u1ed1i c\u00f9ng c\u0169ng kh\u00f4ng th\u1ec3 b\u1ea3o v\u1ec7 cho nh\u00e0 Th\u01b0\u01a1ng kh\u1ecfi b\u1ecb nh\u00e0 Chu thay th\u1ebf.\n\nVi\u1ec7c nh\u00e0 Th\u01b0\u01a1ng di\u1ec7t vong l\u00e0 \u0111\u1ecbnh s\u1ed1 (1). Ch\u00ednh v\u00ec \u0111\u1ecbnh s\u1ed1 \u0111\u00f3, n\u00ean Tr\u1ee5 V\u01b0\u01a1ng d\u1eabu l\u00e0 m\u1ed9t v\u1ecb vua v\u0103n v\u00f5 song to\u00e0n, v\u1eabn s\u1ebd theo \u0111\u1ecbnh s\u1ed1 n\u00e0y m\u00e0 g\u00e2y ra c\u1ea3nh n\u01b0\u1edbc m\u1ea5t nh\u00e0 tan, tr\u1edf n\u00ean d\u00e2m \u0111\u00e3ng \u00e1c \u0111\u1ed9c, b\u1ea5t k\u00ednh N\u1eef Oa, m\u00ea \u0111\u1eafm \u0110\u00e1t K\u1ef7. B\u1edfi v\u00ec n\u1ebfu Tr\u1ee5 V\u01b0\u01a1ng c\u1ee9 t\u00e0i tr\u00ed nh\u01b0 v\u1eady, c\u1ee9 anh minh nh\u01b0 v\u1eady, th\u00ec \u0111\u1ea5t n\u01b0\u1edbc th\u00e1i b\u00ecnh, \u0111\u00e2u c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 s\u1ee5p \u0111\u1ed5 \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c n\u1eefa. Ch\u00ednh l\u00e0 n\u00f3i trong s\u1ed1 m\u1ec7nh c\u1ee7a Tr\u1ee5 V\u01b0\u01a1ng, \u00f4ng ta b\u1eaft bu\u1ed9c ph\u1ea3i ch\u00ecm \u0111\u1eafm trong s\u1eafc d\u1ee5c, b\u1eaft bu\u1ed9c ph\u1ea3i b\u1ecb h\u1ed3 ly tinh chi\u1ebfm x\u00e1c \u0110\u00e1t K\u1ef7 m\u00ea ho\u1eb7c, khi\u1ebfn cho \u00f4ng ta m\u1ea5t \u0111i t\u00e0i n\u0103ng v\u00e0 t\u1ea1o ho\u00e0n c\u1ea3nh cho m\u1ed9t m\u00e0n di\u1ec5n l\u1edbn: Kh\u01b0\u01a1ng T\u1eed Nha phong Th\u1ea7n, V\u0169 V\u01b0\u01a1ng ph\u1ea1t Tr\u1ee5, nh\u00e0 Chu thay th\u1ebf nh\u00e0 Th\u01b0\u01a1ng.\n\n(1): V\u00ec sao l\u1ea1i n\u00f3i s\u1ed1 m\u1ec7nh b\u1eaft bu\u1ed9c nh\u00e0 Th\u01b0\u01a1ng ph\u1ea3i s\u1ee5p \u0111\u1ed5, Tr\u1ee5 V\u01b0\u01a1ng ph\u1ea3i ch\u00ecm \u0111\u1eafm trong s\u1eafc d\u1ee5c ?. C\u00f3 th\u1ec3 n\u00f3i m\u1ed9t \u0111i\u1ec1u v\u00ec h\u1ecd ch\u1ec9 l\u00e0 con t\u1ed1t \u0111\u1ec3 c\u00f3 c\u1edb cho vi\u1ec7c thay \u0111\u1ed5i tri\u1ec1u \u0111\u1ea1i, c\u00f3 c\u1edb \u0111\u1ec3 \u0111\u1ea1o gi\u00e1o c\u1ee7a Nguy\u00ean Thu\u1ef7 Thi\u00ean T\u00f4n th\u1ed1ng nh\u1ea5t to\u00e0n b\u1ed9 \u0111\u1ea1o gi\u00e1o gi\u1edbi h\u1ea1 gi\u1edbi. V\u00e0 c\u00f3 c\u1edb \u0111\u1ec3 phong th\u1ea7n th\u00e0nh l\u1eadp Thi\u00ean \u0110\u00ecnh do Ng\u1ecdc Ho\u00e0ng \u0111\u1ea1i \u0111\u1ebf th\u1ed1ng l\u0129nh!!\n\nT\u1eeb B\u00e0n C\u1ed5 khai thi\u00ean t\u00edch \u0111\u1ecba, ba ng\u00e0n Ti\u00ean Thi\u00ean Ma Th\u1ea7n ng\u0103n c\u1ea3n b\u1ecb B\u00e0n C\u1ed5 to\u00e0n b\u1ed9 ch\u00e9m \u0111\u1ee9t. C\u00f2n c\u00f3 B\u00e0n C\u1ed5 khai thi\u00ean sinh h\u00f3a h\u1ed3ng hoang, th\u1ebf gi\u1edbi H\u1ed3ng Hoang r\u1ed1t c\u1ee5c xu\u1ea5t hi\u1ec7n. Y\u00eau s\u01b0 C\u00f4n B\u1eb1ng, \u0110\u00f4ng Ho\u00e0ng qu\u00e1 m\u1ed9t, T\u1ed5 Vu \u0110\u1ebf Giang, \u0110\u1ecba ti\u00ean chi V\u01b0\u01a1ng Tr\u1ea5n Nguy\u00ean t\u1eed t\u1eebng c\u00e1i t\u1eebng c\u00e1i trong th\u1ea7n tho\u1ea1i nh\u00e2n v\u1eadt ch\u1eadm r\u00e3i xu\u1ea5t hi\u1ec7n. C\u00f2n c\u00f3 thi\u00ean \u0111\u1ecba tam \u0111\u1ea1i chi\u1ebfn, \"Long ph\u01b0\u1ee3ng K\u1ef3 L\u00e2n tam t\u1ed9c \u0111\u1ea1i chi\u1ebfn\" , \"Vu Y\u00eau \u0111\u1ea1i chi\u1ebfn\",v\u00e0 cu\u1ed1i c\u00f9ng l\u00e0 \"Phong Th\u1ea7n \u0111\u1ea1i chi\u1ebfn\". \n\n Sau \u0111\u00f3 Nh\u00e2n T\u1ed9c qu\u1eadt kh\u1edfi t\u1ef1 x\u01b0ng l\u00e0 Thi\u00ean t\u1eed - con c\u1ee7a tr\u1eddi (tr\u01b0\u1edbc \u0111\u00f3, con ng\u01b0\u1eddi d\u01b0\u1edbi tr\u1ecb v\u00ec c\u1ee7a th\u1eddi \u0111\u1ea1i Hi\u00ean Vi\u00ean Ho\u00e0ng \u0111\u1ebf \u0111\u1ea1i chi\u1ebfn Vu Y\u00eau \u0111\u1ee9ng ngang h\u00e0ng v\u1edbi c\u00e1c t\u1ed9c kh\u00e1c, hi\u1ec7n gi\u1edd ch\u1ec9 c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 x\u01b0ng con v\u1edbi Thi\u00ean \u0111\u00ecnh Ng\u1ecdc Ho\u00e0ng ). R\u1ed3i d\u1ea7n d\u1ea7n th\u00e0nh \u00edt d\u00e2n gian Truy\u1ec1n thuy\u1ebft: H\u1eadu Ngh\u1ec7 x\u1ea1 nh\u1eadt, Khoa Ph\u1ee5 \u0111u\u1ed5i m\u1eb7t tr\u1eddi, n\u00e0ng Tinh V\u1ec7 l\u1ea5p bi\u1ec3n, \u0110\u1ea1i V\u0169 tr\u1ecb th\u1ee7y, H\u1eb1ng Nga b\u00f4n nguy\u1ec7t, N\u1eef Oa v\u00e1 thi\u00ean, N\u1eef Oa t\u1ea1o ng\u01b0\u1eddi, \u0111\u1ec3 l\u00e0m n\u1ed5i b\u1eadt n\u00ean h\u00ecnh \u1ea3nh v\u0129 \u0111\u1ea1i c\u1ee7a Thi\u00ean \u0110\u00ecnh. C\u0169ng ch\u1ea5m d\u1ee9t ho\u00e0n to\u00e0n m\u1ed9t h\u1ec7 th\u1ed1ng tri\u1ec1u \u0111\u1ea1i cai tr\u1ecb c\u1ee7a nh\u00e0 Th\u01b0\u01a1ng thay th\u1ebf b\u1eb1ng nh\u00e0 Chu ( mang s\u1ed1 m\u1ec7nh Thi\u00ean t\u1eed ?).\n\nV\u1ec1 ph\u00eda Thi\u00ean \u0110\u00ecnh, tr\u01b0\u1edbc \u0111\u00f3 kh\u00f4ng c\u00f3 m\u1ed9t ai mu\u1ed1n l\u00ean l\u00e0m th\u1ea7n ti\u00ean cho Thi\u00ean \u0110\u00ecnh, c\u00e1i h\u1ecd mu\u1ed1n l\u00e0 s\u1ef1 ti\u00eau dao, v\u00f4 t\u01b0 th\u00edch g\u00ec l\u00e0m n\u1ea5y m\u00e0 kh\u00f4ng b\u1ecb tr\u00f3i bu\u1ed9c hay tr\u00e1ch nhi\u1ec7m qu\u1ea5n th\u00e2n. Sau \"Phong th\u1ea7n \u0111\u1ea1i chi\u1ebfn\" c\u00e1c m\u00f4n h\u1ea1 \u0111\u1ec7 t\u1eed trong Tam Thanh ng\u01b0\u1eddi th\u00ec ch\u1ebft, ng\u01b0\u1eddi th\u00ec b\u1ecb li\u00ean lu\u1ef5 s\u1ed1ng lay l\u1eaft v\u00e0 ph\u1ea3i ph\u00e2n m\u1ed9t tia th\u1ea7n th\u1ee9c-t\u00e0n h\u1ed3n v\u00e0o Phong th\u1ea7n b\u1ea3ng. \u0110i\u1ec1u \u0111\u00f3 khi\u1ebfn l\u1ef1c l\u01b0\u1ee3ng thi\u00ean binh , th\u1ea7n t\u01b0\u1edbng, c\u00e1c quan th\u1ed5 \u0111\u1ecba \"\u0111\u1ecba ph\u01b0\u01a1ng\" \u0111\u00e3 \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c b\u1ed5 sung \u0111\u1ea7y \u0111\u1ee7 sung t\u00fac, \u0111\u1ee7 s\u1ee9c th\u00e0nh l\u1eadp m\u1ed9t h\u1ec7 th\u1ed1ng ho\u00e0n ch\u1ec9nh cai qu\u1ea3n tam gi\u1edbi. \u0110\u1ea1i \u0111\u1ea1o \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c th\u1ed1ng nh\u1ea5t. Phong th\u1ea7n b\u1ea3ng c\u00f2n, th\u1ea7n ti\u00ean \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c phong v\u0129nh sinh b\u1ea5t di\u1ec7t, v\u1ea1n th\u1ebf tr\u01b0\u1eddng t\u1ed3n. C\u0169ng ch\u00ednh v\u00ec th\u1ebf h\u1ecd c\u0169ng v\u0129nh vi\u1ec5n b\u1ecb c\u1ea7m t\u00f9, kh\u00f4ng c\u00f3 t\u01b0 c\u00e1ch l\u00e0m ch\u1ee7 b\u1ea3n th\u00e2n,kh\u00f4ng th\u1ec3 t\u0103ng c\u01b0\u1eddng th\u1ef1c l\u1ef1c (\u0111\u1ebfn m\u1ee9c b\u1ecb m\u1ed9t con kh\u1ec9 m\u1edbi xu\u1ea5t s\u01a1n b\u1eaft n\u1ea1t v\u00e0 ph\u1ea3i ch\u1ecbu n\u00e9n gi\u1eadn cho qua chuy\u1ec7n). V\u00e0 lu\u00f4n ph\u1ea3i ch\u1ecbu s\u1ef1 sai khi\u1ebfn c\u1ee7a ng\u01b0\u1eddi n\u1eafm gi\u1eef Phong th\u1ea7n b\u1ea3ng.\n\nCu\u1ed1i c\u00f9ng, m\u1ecdi th\u1ee9 ch\u1ec9 l\u00e0 qu\u00e2n c\u1edd trong tay Tam thanh \u0111\u1ea5u \u0111\u00e1 l\u1eabn nhau. Tr\u1ee5 V\u01b0\u01a1ng c\u0169ng th\u1ebf, nh\u00e0 Th\u01b0\u01a1ng c\u0169ng th\u1ebf, vi\u1ec7c s\u1eafp \u0111\u1ea1i \u0110\u00e1t K\u1ef7 hay c\u1ea7m t\u00f9 ph\u1ee5 th\u00e2n c\u1ee7a C\u01a1 Ph\u00e1t c\u0169ng th\u1ebf. {"id": 1710128354895286781, "id_str": "1710128354895286781", "url": "https://twitter.com/Blogtravelasia/status/1710128354895286781", "date": "2023-10-06 03:02:27+00:00", "user": {"id": 1692126822195171328, "id_str": "1692126822195171328", "url": "https://twitter.com/Blogtravelasia", "username": "Blogtravelasia", "displayname": "WanderlustJourney", "rawDescription": "It's a passionate traveler \ud83c\udf0d\u2708\ufe0f | Love to exploring the beauty of Vietnam & Asia. Join me as I uncover hidden treasures, share travel tips, and embrace diverse", "created": "2023-08-17 10:51:25+00:00", "followersCount": 1034, "friendsCount": 836, "statusesCount": 3319, "favouritesCount": 4121, "listedCount": 0, "mediaCount": 203, "location": "", "profileImageUrl": "https://pbs.twimg.com/profile_images/1692127431195611136/_shmj8fw_normal.jpg", "profileBannerUrl": "https://pbs.twimg.com/profile_banners/1692126822195171328/1692276362", "protected": null, "verified": false, "blue": true, "blueType": null, "descriptionLinks": [], "_type": "snscrape.modules.twitter.User"}, "lang": "en", "rawContent": "Ha Nam, a serene region located to the south of the capital city, boasts pleasant weather and is blessed with numerous natural attractions. It is not only renowned for its long-standing cultural heritage but is also gaining recognition for its spiritual sites, particularly four famous temples: Tam Chuc, Ba Danh, Phat Quang, and Dia Tang Phi Lai. Though it seemed to have been forgotten by time, the temple named Dia Tang has recently undergone a transformation, attracting numerous travelers from afar to pay their respects and enjoy its scenic beauty. The sense of tranquility at the temple gate, the peaceful beauty, and the simplicity of the surroundings make one feel at ease, as if they are free from worldly troubles.\n\nChua Dia Tang Phi Lai, also known as Chua Dung in local folklore, originated from the ancient name \"Dung\" of Ninh Trung village in Thanh Liem district, Ha Nam province. Local residents pass down the story that the temple was built in the 11th century and consists of over 100 chambers. In the past, King Tran Nghe Tong chose the temple as his place of retreat, and King Tu Duc also visited the temple to seek solace.\n\nAs of now, the temple is nearly a thousand years old and has gradually deteriorated over time. It wasn't until the end of 2015 that Venerable Thich Minh Quang began to undertake restoration efforts and gave it a new name, Dia Tang Phi Lai Tu, signifying that Bodhisattva Dia Tang V\u01b0\u01a1ng had come to this place, attained Buddhahood, and did not return. The ancient temple is situated on a hill overlooking vast rice fields, nestled against a pine-covered hill, surrounded by nature in all four directions. Perhaps this is one of the reasons why the temple was abandoned for a long time, as its remote and lush surroundings made it difficult to access before its renovation and subsequent recognition by tourists today.\n\nHow much does it cost to enter Dia Tang Phi Lai Temple?\nCurrently, Dia Tang Phi Lai Temple does not charge an entrance fee. You can enter the temple grounds freely. Despite recent renovations and improvements, the temple does not charge any fees to Buddhist followers or visitors who come for sightseeing. On hot days, the monks at the temple even lend visitors traditional palm-leaf hats to shield them from the sun and offer them the opportunity to take photographs. If you happen to forget to wear appropriate attire, you can also ask for robes available at the temple.\n\nWhen is the best time to visit Dia Tang Phi Lai Temple?\nThe temple is particularly beautiful during the Lunar New Year, with vibrant flowers adorning its premises. Around the 9th to 10th day of the Lunar New Year, the temple recreates the atmosphere of a traditional Northern Delta countryside market with various distinctive stalls. On important occasions, the temple also organizes many activities, providing an opportunity for both Buddhist devotees and pilgrims to visit. The Vu Lan Festival is celebrated on the 30th of the seventh lunar month, the Mid-Autumn Festival on the 15th of the eighth lunar month, and a special summer retreat program takes place from June to July, allowing those interested in temporarily leaving their daily lives behind to live and engage in spiritual activities alongside the monks, performing good deeds and listening to sermons.\n\nDirections and How to Reach Dia Tang Phi Lai Temple\n is located about 70 kilometers south of Hanoi, and there are two convenient routes for both cars and motorcycles:\n\nBy car: Depart from Hanoi and head towards the Cau Gie - Ninh Binh expressway, leading to Phu Ly, Ha Nam, via National Highway 1A. From there, continue straight for about 12 kilometers, and you'll arrive at the temple. The journey by car takes approximately 1.5 hours.\n\nBy motorcycle: From Hanoi, head to Nuoc Ngam Bus Station, then follow National Highway 1A (the old route) to Van Dien, Thuong Tin, Van Dien Train Station, Phu Xuyen, Cau Gie, and Phu Ly City. Follow Provincial Road 495 to reach the temple. This motorcycle route allows you to experience the scenic countryside and may take around 2 to 2.5 hours, depending on your starting point in Hanoi.\n\nWhat to See and Do at Dia Tang Phi Lai Temple?\nDia Tang Phi Lai Temple offers a serene and tranquil environment for visitors. The temple's perfect blend of architecture and nature creates a unique atmosphere. Behind it lies a lush forest, while nearby, there is a small peaceful pond. Inside the temple grounds, you'll find various types of flowers and plants commonly associated with Buddhist settings. Instead of the moss-covered ancient look, the temple features a calm, subdued brown color, evoking a sense of serenity and detachment from worldly affairs. There's no hustle and bustle, no dust, and it's far removed from the chaos of urban life. Pilgrims and travelers alike come here to find a place of tranquility where they can connect with nature, surrounded by Buddhist devotees and the temple's peaceful ambiance.\n\nKh\u1ed5 H\u1ea3i and the 12 Circles: Passing through the temple gate and entering the courtyard, you'll be pleasantly surprised by the extensive white stone pavement. Instead of the typical red brick flooring found in most temples, Dia Tang is paved with white stones. Adjacent to the courtyard is a sign that reads \"Kh\u1ed5 h\u1ea3i,\" which means \"sea of suffering.\" The 12 circles drawn on the white stones in front of the main hall represent the 12 links of dependent origination, symbolizing meditation practice. All of these elements are clear and deeply connected to the teachings of Buddhism.\n\nDifferent Areas within the Temple: Like many traditional temples in the Red River Delta, Dia Tang Phi Lai Temple features traditional architectural elements such as wooden columns and curved roofs with intricate carvings. The most prominent structure within the temple complex is Tam Bao, which is the largest hall dedicated to Bodhisattva Dia Tang. To the right of this hall is the Ancestors' Hall, where 42 founding monks of the temple are venerated. Additionally, there is a small temple dedicated to Bodhisattva Quan The Am, Lord, and Saint Hien. The temple also provides accommodation for monks, Buddhist followers staying at the temple, a lecture hall for daily teachings by the resident monk, and a guesthouse for travelers and participants in temple activities.\n\nView Ancient L\u00fd - Tr\u1ea7n Dynasty Artifacts: The temple houses nearly 100 ceramic, porcelain, and earthenware artifacts with diverse colors, patterns, and motifs, which are identified as relics from the Tran era, with a few rare pieces from the L\u00fd and L\u00ea dynasties. Among them, many roof tiles are engraved with intricate lotus patterns, dragon motifs, and phoenix designs, along with the two parts of a mythical creature that symbolizes historical continuity from the L\u00fd - Tr\u1ea7n era.\n\nThe Path to the Mountain Peak: Conquering the temple's mountain peaks through the steep and challenging path along a stream requires determination. It includes rope-assisted climbs and passages through caves. Along the way, there are nearly 20 resting points for travelers. Meditation gardens are adorned with white stones or lush green grass, providing a space for tea enjoyment, relaxation, and panoramic views of the temple from above. At the Phi Lai peak, you will also find the Pho Dong Tower, built during the L\u00fd - Tr\u1ea7n era, which serves as a resting place for 40 generations of Zen masters.\n\nTips and Etiquette for Visiting Dia Tang Phi Lai Temple:\n\nDress appropriately: Before visiting the temple, ensure you are dressed modestly and avoid revealing attire, as it shows respect for the sacredness of the place. If you forget to wear suitable clothing, you can borrow robes provided by the temple.\n\nRespect temple property: All items and areas within the temple grounds are considered sacred. Do not touch or take any items without the permission of the temple authorities.\n\nOffering donations: Instead of offering money directly to the Buddha statues or altars, it is recommended to place your donation in the designated donation box for accumulating merit.\n\nGreetings: Show respect to the monks and nuns by greeting them with a polite gesture of placing your palms together and bowing.\n\nPhotography: You are generally allowed to take photographs within the temple grounds, but if you plan to use specialized equipment or fly drones for aerial shots, it's advisable to seek permission from the temple management.\n\nChua Dia Tang Phi Lai T\u1ef1 is a spiritual haven that has become an integral part of the lives of the people of Ninh Trung and Liem Son, as well as a spiritual pilgrimage site for visitors from afar. On the first day of each month, on full moon days, or during Buddhist holidays, people from all walks of life visit the temple to offer incense and seek peace and good health, a tradition that has persisted for many years.\n\nDia Tang Phi Lai Temple also plays a significant role in hosting weddings. Couples who choose to marry at the temple are embracing deep spiritual meaning. It's a practice that signifies respect for Buddhist traditions and emphasizes harmony, compassion, and love\u2014an ethos that Buddhism encourages.\n\nThe H\u1eb1ng Thu\u1eadn Festival, celebrated at Dia Tang Phi Lai Temple, is an important occasion for the Buddhist community to gather and engage in spiritual practice. This festival typically takes place on the 1st day of the 1st lunar month each year, coinciding with an anniversary in the life of the Buddha. The festival includes religious activities such as paying homage to the Buddha, prayers, and acts of charity, such as giving \n\n#DiaTangPhiLaiTemple\n#HaNam #SpiritualRetreat #BuddhistHeritage\n#TranquilEscape #CulturalExperience\n#HistoricalSite #VietnameseCulture\n#TempleJourney #PeacefulOasis\n#TravelVietnam #HiddenGem #BuddhistTradition\n#VietnameseSpirituality #Tranquility\n#TempleDiscovery #ExploreVietnam\n#SacredPlace #CulturalHeritage\n#SereneEnvironment", "replyCount": 49, "retweetCount": 2, "likeCount": 70, "quoteCount": 0, "conversationId": 1710128354895286781, "hashtags": [], "cashtags": [], "mentionedUsers": [], "links": [], "viewCount": 1303, "retweetedTweet": null, "quotedTweet": null, "place": null, "coordinates": null, "inReplyToTweetId": null, "inReplyToUser": null, "source": "<a href=\"https://mobile.twitter.com\" rel=\"nofollow\">Twitter Web App</a>", "sourceUrl": "https://mobile.twitter.com", "sourceLabel": "Twitter Web App", "media": {"photos": [], "videos": [{"thumbnailUrl": "https://pbs.twimg.com/ext_tw_video_thumb/1710126415834963968/pu/img/HKqi1dtyts1bYAJ9.jpg", "variants": [{"contentType": "video/mp4", "bitrate": 2176000, "url": "https://video.twimg.com/ext_tw_video/1710126415834963968/pu/vid/avc1/1280x720/VpHcSoOFxADQDI90.mp4?tag=12"}, {"contentType": "video/mp4", "bitrate": 832000, "url": "https://video.twimg.com/ext_tw_video/1710126415834963968/pu/vid/avc1/640x360/iE8KH0zXTQ1PDwYz.mp4?tag=12"}, {"contentType": "video/mp4", "bitrate": 256000, "url": "https://video.twimg.com/ext_tw_video/1710126415834963968/pu/vid/avc1/480x270/69EnhZ0gy35Oeth6.mp4?tag=12"}], "duration": 71966, "views": null}], "animated": []}, "_type": "snscrape.modules.twitter.Tweet"}

Nhi\u1ec7m v\u1ee5 ch\u00ednh c\u1ee7a SEC l\u00e0 b\u1ea3o v\u1ec7 c\u00e1c nh\u00e0 \u0111\u1ea7u t\u01b0, \u0111\u1ea3m b\u1ea3o s\u1ef1 minh b\u1ea1ch v\u00e0 c\u00f4ng b\u1eb1ng trong th\u1ecb tr\u01b0\u1eddng t\u00e0i ch\u00ednh, v\u00e0 \u00e1p d\u1ee5ng c\u00e1c quy t\u1eafc v\u00e0 quy \u0111\u1ecbnh \u0111\u1ec3 \u0111\u1ea3m b\u1ea3o ho\u1ea1t \u0111\u1ed9ng c\u1ee7a th\u1ecb tr\u01b0\u1eddng di\u1ec5n ra theo quy \u0111\u1ecbnh v\u00e0 an to\u00e0n.\n\nS\u1ef1 \u1ea3nh h\u01b0\u1edfng c\u1ee7a SEC \u0111\u1ebfn gi\u00e1 Bitcoin (BTC) th\u01b0\u1eddng li\u00ean quan \u0111\u1ebfn quy\u1ebft \u0111\u1ecbnh v\u00e0 ph\u00e1t bi\u1ec3u c\u1ee7a h\u1ecd v\u1ec1 vi\u1ec7c \u0111i\u1ec1u ch\u1ec9nh ho\u1eb7c gi\u00e1m s\u00e1t c\u00e1c s\u1ea3n ph\u1ea9m li\u00ean quan \u0111\u1ebfn ti\u1ec1n \u0111i\u1ec7n t\u1eed v\u00e0 th\u1ecb tr\u01b0\u1eddng ch\u1ee9ng kho\u00e1n. C\u1ee5 th\u1ec3:\n\n\ud83d\udc49Quy\u1ebft \u0111\u1ecbnh v\u1ec1 ETF (Exchange-Traded Fund): SEC th\u01b0\u1eddng ph\u1ea3i xem x\u00e9t v\u00e0 quy\u1ebft \u0111\u1ecbnh v\u1ec1 vi\u1ec7c cho ph\u00e9p ho\u1eb7c t\u1eeb ch\u1ed1i vi\u1ec7c th\u00e0nh l\u1eadp c\u00e1c qu\u1ef9 ETF li\u00ean quan \u0111\u1ebfn ti\u1ec1n \u0111i\u1ec7n t\u1eed nh\u01b0 Bitcoin. C\u00e1c lo\u1ea1i ph\u1ed5 bi\u1ebfn nh\u01b0 b\u1ea1c h\u00e0, h\u00fang qu\u1ebf, h\u00fang c\u00e2y, oregano, v\u00e0 ng\u00f2 gai \u0111\u1ec1u c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 th\u00edch \u1ee9ng v\u1edbi \u0111i\u1ec1u ki\u1ec7n kh\u00ed h\u1eadu v\u00e0 v\u1ecb tr\u00ed kh\u00e1c nhau.\n\n2\ufe0f\u20e3. Th\u00eam ch\u00fat b\u1ea1c h\u00e0 t\u01b0\u01a1i v\u00e0o m\u1ed9t ly n\u01b0\u1edbc tr\u00e0 \u1ea5m s\u1ebd t\u1ea1o ra m\u1ed9t m\u00f9i th\u01a1m tinh t\u1ebf v\u00e0 c\u00f3 l\u1ee3i cho s\u1ee9c kh\u1ecfe. L\u00e0m S\u1ea1ch Kh\u00f4ng Kh\u00ed: \nNghi\u00ean c\u1ee9u NASA \u0111\u00e3 ch\u1ee9ng minh r\u1eb1ng c\u00e2y l\u1ee5c th\u1ea3o c\u00f3 kh\u1ea3 n\u0103ng l\u00e0m s\u1ea1ch kh\u00f4ng kh\u00ed b\u1eb1ng c\u00e1ch lo\u1ea1i b\u1ecf c\u00e1c ch\u1ea5t \u0111\u1ed9c h\u1ea1i nh\u01b0 Xylen, Carbon, Fomandehit, v\u00e0 Benzen. \u0110i\u1ec1u n\u00e0y gi\u00fap c\u1ea3i thi\u1ec7n ch\u1ea5t l\u01b0\u1ee3ng kh\u00f4ng kh\u00ed trong nh\u00e0.\n\n4\ufe0f\u20e3.
